Fifteen Japanese War Criminals Innocent

— Chi Fu

On the eve of the second anniversary of Japan's surrender and signing, General MacArthur announced another "benevolent government" for Japan. That is the United Press International's August 31 Tokyo telegram: "Five former Japanese cabinet members, including one admiral, one false army general, one leader of the zaibatsu, and ten other major war criminals who have not yet been tried, were released from Sugamo Prison on the 30th."

When these war criminals were released from prison, they asked the prison authorities one after another: "Released! Is it really true?" Everyone was overjoyed and thanked General MacArthur's holy virtue.

When the news spread to the world, everyone was half believing and half doubting. Believing was MacArthur's arbitrariness and his policy of indulging Japan, there must be such a thing, but indulging too much and it was not the right time; doubting was that the "spirit" of the Potsdam Declaration was not to be destroyed by the defeated countries, and not to be destroyed by the United Nations, but by the unilateral destruction of the United States. In the future peace conference with Japan, how will the Allied countries speak? How will the terms of the future peace treaty with Japan be written? It's really puzzling.

To be fair, General MacArthur's release of this group of war criminals was indeed a wrong measure, and people of the Allied countries should protest! In particular, the Allied prosecutor (the Chinese prosecutor is Xiang Zhejun) announced that this group of war criminals would not be prosecuted, which is extremely absurd, and people of the supervisory countries should protest! Now we introduce the resumes of this group of "innocent" invaders, and let fair readers judge:

Ayukawa Yoshisuke Japan's top chaebol is the industrial dictator of "Manchukuo", former president of Japan Sishi, member of the House of Peers. He is the mastermind of "Manchuria's" economic invasion, the mainstream of Japan's military-industrial production

Kobayashi Jizo Active Admiral, former Vice Minister of the Navy, Commander of the Combined Fleet, Governor of Taiwan, Chairman of the Central Cooperation Council, Zeng Zhengzeng Director, former Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Koiso Cabinet. During her tenure as Governor of Taiwan, she used Taiwan as a base to invade China and the Pacific. She is the soul of the Japanese Navy.

Masaki Jinzaburo Reserve Army General, Military Councilor. She is the leader of the "February 26 Incident", the fierce faction of the early "young" Japanese, and has created many incidents, all of which are related to launching aggression.

Murata Shozo Former Minister of Communications in the Kondo Cabinet, Ambassador to the Philippine puppet government during the Pacific War.

Otatsu Shigeo Former Minister of Home Affairs in the Tojo Cabinet, Mayor of "Shonan" (Singapore) during the Pacific War, and tried to eliminate British influence.

Sakai Tadamasa Former Minister of Agriculture and Forestry in the Abe Cabinet.

Matsuzaka Zheng Former Minister of Justice in the Tojo Cabinet.

Okabe Nagakage Former Minister of Education in the Tojo Cabinet.

Ota Kozo Former professor of Hosei University, Director-General of the Taisei Yokosankai, served as Minister of Education.

Shoriki Matsutaro Former President of Tokyo Yomiuri Shimbun, she is the spokesperson of the Japanese military department, the publisher of the newspaper that has the strongest support for secondary aggression

Kobayashi Junichiro Former Director-General of the Taisei Yokosankai, she is a colonel.

Kikuchi Takeo She is a member of the House of Peers who was born as a lieutenant general. She is an extreme "patriot" and the most vocal person attacking the "Emperor Organ Theory".

Okura Kunihiko She is the founder of the Okura Institute of Mental Science and the president of the Shanghai Tongwen Hospital of Toyo University. She is a powerful supporter of the "spiritual science" of Japanese aggression. Many Japanese executives who ruled the "Wang regime" were her students.

Shindo Kazuma President of the "Genyosha", the leader of Japanese theocracy and all reactionary elements.

Ida Keinan Former member of the House of Peers, leader of extreme "patriotism"

Traveling in the United States, Miscellaneous Record, Xu Zi

The Positive Effect of Hot Water Bags

In the minds of American writers, Chinese women have extraordinary wisdom. They use the rubber bags commonly found in hospitals as hand warmers, and for a period of time, it became a trend. Almost all women have a bag in their hearts, and the colors of the bags are also divided into gold, silver, red, gray, green, pink, etc., plus a square silk handkerchief, just like icing on the cake. American women would never think so thoughtfully and fascinatingly. The original function of the warm bag is to dispel pain from tumors in the hospital. If you have a tumor in any part of your body, the doctor will give you a rubber bag filled with warm water and apply it to the affected area several times a day. After three to five days, the swelling will subside and the pain will stop. If you feel uncomfortable with hot water in summer, you can switch to ice water. Ice water has the same anti-swelling effect. This treatment is extremely popular in Chinese folk customs, but there are no hot water bags in the countryside. They use a spatula for cooking. They heat the spatula in a pot and gently strike the affected area several times a day. After striking, the patient feels scorched and uncomfortable, and after striking a few times, the swelling and pain will be relieved. This folk method is considered superstitious by Chinese-style Western doctors. How can a knife cure the disease? In fact, it is not the knife that cures the disease, but the heat. When American exporters packed a large number of hot water bags to China, the American medical community was greatly surprised when they saw the number of hot water bags exported in the export goods. They thought that Chinese medicine had developed so rapidly, and so many hot water bags were used, and other sanitary products could be imagined. Later, they specially sent several medical authorities to China to investigate hygiene undertakings and found that Chinese women all carried a hot water bag, and they couldn't help laughing to themselves. After returning to the United States, one of the authorities wrote a wonderful book, praising the intelligence of Chinese women. There are many clever things Chinese people do, such as tightening the legs of the quilt cover to hold rice, using the bathtub as a boat, Nanjing people modified the three-wheeled machine foot road army into an eight-seater passenger car, using firecrackers as DDT, pasting movie newspapers on walls, and using banknotes to light cigarettes, all of which are creative and economical.

The above figures were all arrested by General MacArthur after September 12, 1945. After two years without trial, the prosecutor of the Far East International Military Tribunal announced that they were "innocent" and released. Is it reasonable? Let the readers judge!

The Japanese People Discuss MacArthur

— Translated by Bao Zhongqi

[Translator's Note] An American magazine reporter interviewed Japanese people, asking, "What is your impression of MacArthur?" Their answers were almost uniformly praising MacArthur first, then lamenting their suffering to gain the sympathy and aid of Americans. The cunning Japanese people!

Student: Most Japanese people believe that the current military control is beneficial to our country. MacArthur is a genius, and you Americans should support him. Unfortunately, the food supply is poor. This year is a matter of life and death. There is a lack of housing. You will often find five or six families living in one room.

Hotel Clerk: Every Japanese person thinks MacArthur is a good man. We have hope and hope that your army will continue to stay here until the Japanese can be self-sufficient. First, you must help us eliminate the black market. Everything is too expensive. The value of sugar has exceeded that of jewels.

Travel Agent: All Japanese people are extremely pleased that you sent MacArthur to our country. The Soviet Union would not treat me so kindly. We hope that Americans will sponsor us to restore our pre-war state. Food and clothing are insufficient except when obtained through the black market.

Newspaper Boy: Prices are too high. I hope this is the peak. However, American officials treat me so kindly. I am willing to work for them. I hope I can meet MacArthur.

Grocery Store Owner: Living conditions are better than a year ago. Food is still lacking, and so is clothing. A year ago, we had nothing. MacArthur gave people jobs. We urgently need free trade. We love and need America.

Jeweler: I want to see prices drop. Under military control, the general situation is better. I understand Americans. I have been trading with them for twenty years. They are good people, just like MacArthur. I hope to be able to trade freely again immediately. Japan needs it.

Merchant: National expenditure is three to four hundred times higher than before the war. We hope you can stay here until we can be self-sufficient. We fear the Soviet Union. We need MacArthur's protection. He will prevent the Soviet Union from repeating on our country what it did to European countries.

Old Bookstore Owner: Living conditions are very bad. The black market is causing us to struggle painfully. We need more help. We need America. Only MacArthur can satisfy the inadequate strength of our government.

Please Postpone the Dancing Ban

— Li Ling

Dancing, in civilized countries in Europe and America, is originally a proper form of entertainment and common social activity between men and women. However, like an orange north of the Huai River turning into a bitter orange, once it comes to China, it changes its nature, becoming a profession that allows those pitiful people struggling on the brink of starvation to survive. The reason for this change in nature need not be concealed; it is a serious problem of the current society that is not simple. The change in the nature of dancing is just a subtle manifestation of the society’s unhealthy phenomena.

Is the reason why dance hostesses are dance hostesses because they willingly use their physical appearance to gain the favor of young masters? Are they willingly degenerate and refuse to engage in productive work? When we look around, the young men and women who are unemployed upon graduation have the ambition and intention to participate in productive work, to serve the country and society, and to strive for their own future. However, the productive sectors of society are currently too few. Even this group of pure and promising young men and women with knowledge cannot be accommodated, let alone our group of dance hostesses and practitioners who lack production skills, insufficient intelligence, and inadequate ability.

Some people say, "The life of a dance hostess is too extravagant." This is a fact that we do not deny. However, extravagant dance hostesses are actually only a minority. More than ninety percent of us engage in the dance industry at night and take care of household chores during the day. Those with children also have to take care of their children and bear the double burden of being a housewife and a working woman. If one only sees the few extravagant dance hostesses and assumes that all dance hostesses are extravagant, that is tantamount to saying, "Schools ask for money, so education is undesirable."

Banning dancing will not only increase the number of unemployed people in Shanghai by more than 20,000 but will also exacerbate the unemployment problem that society urgently needs to solve but cannot. As the ancient saying goes, "Only when clothing and food are sufficient can one know honor and shame." If society truly had a way to maintain our livelihood, the government would not need to ban dancing, and we would automatically change our profession. Conversely, even if the government orders a ban on dancing, it will only create the tragic fate of more than 20,000 people in reality! We hope that the wise government will postpone the implementation of the ban, allowing us a chance to catch our breath and change our profession at ease. (Note: Ms. Li is one of the directors of the Shanghai Dance Hostess Association.)

"Free Talk" Over Thirty-Six Years

— Zheng Fan

From April 1, the ninth year of the Republic of China, to November 30, the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, this considerably long period of twelve years was hosted by Zhou Shoujuan. Those who wrote for "Free Talk" were all the famous so-called "Saturday School" literati of the time in Shanghai. The content was nothing more than "talking about love," "romanticizing nature," and "broadly discussing various topics." At one point, the pages were divided into categories such as "Idle Talk," "Miscellany," "Miscellaneous Things Heard," "Travel Notes," "Drama Talk," "Leftovers," and "Trivia." In addition, lengthy serialized chapters of novels and anecdotes about the literary scene never ceased.

This style did not undergo a sudden change until Li Liewen took over "Free Talk" at the end of the twenty-first year, and the one who inherited this mantle was the newly created "Spring and Autumn Supplement," still hosted by Zhou Shoujuan.

The period when Li Liewen edited "Free Talk," although only a short year and five months, broke through the past style of "Free Talk," writing in another direction, deeply influencing the literary youth of the time. At that time, it was indeed a "Free Talk" and also an important page in the modern Chinese literary history!

At that time, Mr. Liang Cai, the general manager of this newspaper's history, was actively improving the newspaper. Coincidentally, Li Liewen had just returned from France, and he was hired to the newspaper to edit "Free Talk." Li's first shot after taking over was to cut off the serialized novel "The Crossroads of the Times and Love" by Zhang Ziping. Zhang Ziping's novel therefore declined greatly in popularity. Li Liewen completely turned "Free Talk" into a base for new literature, and almost all of the first-class writers in China at the time were captured by "Free Talk." Those who regularly contributed included Lu Xun, Yu Dafu, Mao Dun, Lao She, etc. At the same time, because he paid attention to essays, he promoted many new writers, such as Kang Qiang and Kong Lingjing.

Precisely because the writing of "Free Talk" at that time had an explosive nature, an announcement was finally posted, "Allowed to Talk About Love Affairs," and the style became slightly more bland, but the writers were still the original team. Among them, Lu Xun used many pen names due to special relationships. The more commonly used ones were "He Jia Gan," "Leisure," "Congee," "Lühua," and "Luo Wen." Later, because it was inconvenient for him to come forward himself, he simply wrote articles, asked people to copy them, and added a pen name, so even the editors were deceived. These texts were later included by Lu Xun in "False Freedom Book," "Allowed Love Affairs Talk," and "Fringe Literature."

During that time, there were several major debates, such as the problem of students reading Zhuangzi's selected works, the problem of mass language, and even the problem of humor and the problem of sons-in-law, all of which were very famous and can be seen in everyone's essays.

In May of the twenty-third year, Li resigned and was succeeded by Zhang Zisheng (May 9), returning from splendor to plainness until the cessation of publication on November 1 of the twenty-fourth year.

During the Anti-Japanese War, the Shenbao was once moved to Hankou and Hong Kong for publication. "Free Talk" was also published some of the time during the year or so in Hong Kong. In the tenth month of the twenty-seventh year of the Republic of China, the Shenbao was republished in Shanghai, and "Free Talk" was hosted by "Wang Renshu," still with a "Lu Xun style."

Soon, Hu Shanyuan changed the editorship, and the writers were mostly young literati, such as Ding Di and Wen Zongshan, and the style became even more bland. After more than a year, Huang Jiayin edited it, specializing in Western essays and scientific interest, with the same style as his Western Breeze Magazine.

Thus, until December 8 of the thirty-first year, the Pacific War broke out, and the newspaper was suspended.

After the victory, the Shenbao gloriously resumed publication in Shanghai. "Free Talk" was initially edited by Huang Jiayin, and in May of last year, it was edited by Bu Shaofu, the deputy editor-in-chief of this newspaper. In February of this year, Qian Taisheng took over the editorship and has continued until now.

There is no need to say more about everything concerning "Free Talk" at present. One point to add here is that "Free Talk" was originally a garden for new literature, but after the victory, it was transplanted to "Spring and Autumn." "Free Talk" specializes in newsy, educational, scientific, knowledge-based, and interesting essays. As mentioned above, although the style and content of "Free Talk" have changed repeatedly, there is only one principle: it is always a truly "Free Talk," free and unrestrained, without prejudice or restraint! (To be continued)
